()1. action="rule:..." Ka Syntax Kya Hai?
SailPoint me jab aap kisi <Step> ke andar action attribute lagate hain, 
to aap rule: keyword ke baad us Rule ka asli naam likhte hain jo aapne SailPoint ke database me pehle se import kiya hua hai.
Aapka Case: Aapne likha hai rule:Account Invite, iska matlab system database me jayega aur
<Rule name="Account Invite" ...> ko dhoodh kar use fire kar dega.
*////////////
  <!-- STEP 4: CONFIRMATION STEP (Safe Session Modification without full Serialization Crash) -->
  <Step icon="Default" name="Confirmation step" posX="380" posY="140">
    <Arg name="response" value="ref:response"/>
    <Script>
      <Source> 
        import javax.faces.application.FacesMessage;
        import java.util.ArrayList;
        import java.util.List;

        List myMessages = new ArrayList();
        int statusCode = 500; // Default fallback error

        if (response != null &amp;&amp; response.get("statusCode") != null) {
            statusCode = (Integer) response.get("statusCode");
        }

        if (statusCode == 200) {
            FacesMessage myMessage = new FacesMessage(
                FacesMessage.SEVERITY_INFO,
                "Account Invite sent successfully.",
                "Account Invite sent successfully."
            );
            myMessages.add(myMessage);
        } else {
            FacesMessage myMessage = new FacesMessage(
                FacesMessage.SEVERITY_ERROR,  
                "Account Invite failed to send. Please check your inputs.",
                "Account Invite failed to send. Please check your inputs."
            );
            myMessages.add(myMessage);
        }

        // Safe execution context lookup for UI messaging lifecycle
        if (httpSession != null) {
            httpSession.setAttribute("sailpoint.web.PageCodeBase.sessionMessages", myMessages);
        }
      </Source> 
    </Script>
    <Transition to="Stop"/>
  </Step>

  <!-- STEP 5: STOP -->
  <Step icon="Stop" name="Stop" posX="500" posY="82"/>

</Workflow>
///////////*
()1. Lifecycle Workflows (LCM):-
Ye sabse zyada use hone wale workflows hain, jo kisi Identity ke lifecycle events par trigger hote hain. 
Jab bhi kisi user ka status change hota hai, ye back-end par provisioning ya notifications handle karte hain.

1. Lifecycle Workflows (LCM):-
Ye sabse zyada use hone wale workflows hain, jo kisi Identity ke lifecycle events par trigger hote hain. Jab bhi kisi user ka status change hota hai, ye back-end par provisioning ya notifications handle karte hain.

-->LCM Lifecycle Trampoline: Jab bhi koi Lifecycle Event (Joiner, Mover, Leaver) fire hota hai, ye workflow check karta hai ki kaun sa specific sub-workflow chalana hai.

-->LCM Provisioning: Kisi bhi access request, role assignment, ya account creation ke baad actual provisioning (Active Directory, JDBC, etc. me account create/modify karna) yahi workflow sambhalta hai.

-->LCM Registration: Naye users ke self-registration process ko manage karne ke liye.  
SailPoint Product Documentation

-->Identity Update / Refresh: Jab IdentityRefresh task chalta hai aur koi attribute change detect hota hai, tab ye trigger ho sakta hai.

2. Access Request Workflows:-
User jab IdentityIQ ke Dashboard se koi access (Entitlement ya Role) request karta hai, tab ye workflows picture mein aate hain.

-->Manager Approval Workflow: Request submit hone ke baad approval ke liye sabse pehle manager ke paas bhejne ka logic.  
SailPoint Product Documentation

-->Owner Approval Workflow: Agar kisi requested Role ya Application ka koi specific owner hai, to uske approval ke liye approval item create karna.

-->Multi-Approve Workflow: Jab ek se zyada levels (Manager -> Owner -> Security Officer) par approvals ki zaroorat hoti hai.

3. Certification / Compliance Workflows
Identity Certification (User Access Review) ke dauran jab koi reviewer kisi ka access Revoke (remit) karta hai, ya certification end hoti hai, tab ye workflows back-end par automatic action lete hain.

-->Certification Provisioning: Certification me jab access revoke kiya jata hai, to target system se us access ka account/entitlement remove karne ke liye ye workflow chalaya jata hai.

-->Certification Remediation: Access automatically remove karne ke bajay agar kisi ticket system (like ServiceNow) me ticket raise karna ho.

4. Account Aggregation & Policy Violations Workflows:-
Ye workflows data ingestion aur risk/compliance checks ke dauran kaam aate hain.

-->Target Aggregation Workflow: Jab target system se accounts aggregate ho rahe hon aur kisi specific condition par custom logic chalana ho.

-->Policy Violation Workflow: Agar koi SOD (Segregation of Duties) ya Activity Policy violate hoti hai, 
to ticket generate karne, manager ko alert bhejne, ya automatic remediation ke liye ye workflow use hota hai.

5. System & Custom Workflows:-
Inka use standard IAM flows se alag, background automation ya maintenance ke liye kiya jata hai.

-->Sub-Workflows (Reusable Workflows): Chote workflows jo bade workflows ke andar se call kiye jaate hain (e.g., Email Notification send karna, ya ticket create karna). Isse code redundancy kam hoti hai.

-->Scheduled Workflows / Run Rule: Aise custom workflows jinko aap kisi specific time par chalane ke liye task ke through schedule kar sakte hain.
*///////////
////////////*
1. Ye hai kya?
<Variable name="response"/> ek standard workflow-level variable hai jise Workflow Context mein pure execution ke dauran data 
hold karne ke liye use kiya jata hai.
Jab bhi koi approval process chalta hai (jaise Manager ya Owner ke paas approval ke liye request jaati hai), 
to saamne wala user us request ko Approve karta hai ya Reject. Us approval action ka jo result hota hai, 
use store karne ke liye standard practice ke mutabik response naam ka variable banaya jata hai.
Iska data type generally string hota hai, aur iski common values hoti hain:-
-->approve
-->reject
-->cancel

()value koun dega <Variable name="response"/> ko toh:-
A. Approval Step ya Form se (User Input)
Jab workflow mein ek Approval step define hota hai,aur wo step kisi Work Item(Form) ke throw manager ya owner ke dashboard par 
jata hai, tab jab user click karta hai, to SailPoint back-end par is variable ko populate karta hai.

XML mein ye kuch aisa dikhta hai:-
XML
<Approval name="Manager Approval" owner="ref:managerName" return="response">
  </Approval>
Kaun de raha hai? End-user (Manager/Owner) jab UI par "Approve" ya "Reject" button dabata hai.

B. Workflow ke Sub-Workflow ya Step script se (System/Rule)
Kayi baar hum manual approval ke bajay automatic checks lagate hain. 
Agar koi custom Beanshell script ya Rule chal raha hai, to developer khud wfcontext ka use karke isme value set karta hai.

Java
// Beanshell Script ke andar manually value set karna
if (someCondition) {
    workflow.put("response", "approve");
} else {
    workflow.put("response", "reject");
}Kaun de raha hai? Aapka likha hua Beanshell code ya Rule logic.
---------------------------------------------------------------------
()1. <Variable initializer="false" name="isValid"/>:-
Ye kya hai? Ye ek boolean flag variable hai. Iski shuruati value (initializer) false set ki gayi hai.
Iska kaam kya hai? Isko generally Validation Steps mein use kiya jata hai. 
Jab workflow shuru hota hai, to hum maan ke chalte hain ki data abhi validate nahi hua hai (isValid = false).

Real Project Use Case: Workflow ke pehle ya doosre step mein ek Beanshell script chalti hai jo inputs 
(jaise user attributes, requested roles) ko check karti hai. Agar saari conditions match ho jaati hain, 
to script ke andar isko true set kar diya jata hai:-

Java
if (identity != null && identity.getAttribute("manager") != null) {
    workflow.put("isValid", true);
}
Iske baad workflow transitions mein check hota hai ki agar isValid true hai, 
to hi provisioning par jao, nahi to workflow ko stop kar do.
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
2. <Variable initializer="new java.util.ArrayList()" name="validationErrors"/>:-
Ye kya hai? Ye Java ki ArrayList class ka ek object hai jo workflow context mein initialize ho raha hai.

Iska kaam kya hai? Ye ek khali list (bucket) taiyar karta hai jismein pooray workflow execution ke dauran aane wali validation
errors ya custom error messages ko store kiya ja sake.

Real Project Use Case: Maan lijiye aapke isValid check ke dauran manager missing mila, ya email format galat mila. 
To aap workflow ko directly crash karne ke bajay is list mein error daal dete hain:-

Java
if (identity.getAttribute("email") == null) {
    validationErrors.add("Email attribute cannot be null for identity: " + identity.getName());
}
Baad mein is validationErrors list ko email notification template mein bhej diya jata hai taaki administrator ya manager ko pata 
chal sake ki request kyun fail hui.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
3. <Variable initializer="string:false" name="transient"/>:-Ye kya hai? 
transient SailPoint workflow ka ek Reserved System Variable hai.
Default Behavior: By default, agar aap kisi workflow mein transient define nahi karte ya use true rakhte hain, 
to SailPoint us workflow ke steps ko memory (RAM) mein chalata hai aur khatam kar deta hai. 
Database (identityiq.spt_workflow_case) mein uska koi track ya history save nahi hoti.

string:false Set Karne Se Kya Hoga? Jab aapne isko false set kar diya, 
to iska matlab hai ki ab ye workflow Transient NAHI hai (Non-Transient hai).

Iska fayda ye hota hai:-
Database Persistence: Workflow Case ka poora data aur steps database mein save honge.
Work Item References: Agar is workflow ke andar koi Approval step aata hai (jo kisi Manager ke paas approval ke liye jayega), 
to SailPoint ek background WorkItem generate karega. Agar workflow transient hota, 
to work item generate hote hi workflow terminate ho jata kyunki wo database mein state save nahi kar pata. 
Non-transient hone ki wajah se workflow 'Suspend' state mein wait kar sakta hai jab tak manager dashboard par jaakar action na le.
Task Manager Visibility: Aap IdentityIQ UI -> Administrator -> Advanced -> Workflow Cases mein jaakar is chalte hue ya complete
hue workflow ka live status trace kar sakte hain.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
()<Variable name="flow"/> kya hai?
SailPoint IdentityIQ (IIQ) workflow XML mein <Variable name="flow"/> 
bhi ek behad important System-Reserved Variable ya fir Contextual Variable hota hai.
Iska use ye janne ke liye kiya jata hai ki kisi user par kaun sa specific identity lifecycle event chal raha hai 
(jaise Joiner, Mover, Leaver) ya fir <Variable name="flow"/> workflow ka wo directional compass hai jo engine ko batata hai ki 
identity ke upar chalne wala operation kis type ka hai (Joiner, Mover, Leaver, ya AccessRequest).

1. Is variable ko value kaun deta hai? (Who provides the value?)
Is variable ko value aapko manually nahi deni padti. Jab bhi koi Lifecycle Event trigger hota hai ya IdentityRefresh task chalta hai, 
to SailPoint ka internal engine (LCM Lifecycle Trampoline ya Identity Lifecycle process) automatic is variable ke andar event ka
naam populate kar deta hai.

2. Iske common Standard Values kya hain?
--Project ke standard implementation mein flow variable ke andar ye standard string values aati hain:

--AccessRequest: Jab koi user khud ke liye ya manager kisi subordinate ke liye dashboard se access request submit karta hai.

--IdentityLifecycle-Joiner: Jab HR system (jaise Workday) se koi naya record aggregate hota hai aur naya user create hota hai.

--IdentityLifecycle-Mover: Jab kisi existing user ka Department, Job Title, ya Manager change hota hai.

--IdentityLifecycle-Leaver: Jab koi employee company chhodta hai (Termination/Separation).

--AccountsRequest: Jab direct kisi target application par account action request kiya jaye.
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
()owner="script:return context.getUserName();":-
Khud Ka Form, Khud Hi Owner: context.getUserName() lagane se workflow ye ensure karta hai 
ki jis Public Officer ne button dabaya hai, ye form usi ki screen par khule aur wahi ise submit kar sake.
Security Guard: Isse ye security milti hai ki koi dusra logged-in user galti se ya shararat me is specific work item ko open,
edit ya submit nahi kar sakta. Yeh form poori tarah se usi launcher ke liye lock ho jata hai.

1. <WorkItemConfig> (The Configuration Box):-
Kya karta hai: Yeh SailPoint ka ek container tag hai. Yeh workflow ko batata hai ki, 
"Niche jo bhi settings likhi hain, unka use is step ke liye banne wale Work Item (Task/Form) ki extra properties aur alerts ko
manage karne ke liye kiya jaye." * Iske andar aap email notification, reminders, ya escalation jaisi settings configure karte hain.

2. <NotificationEmailTemplateRef> (The Alert Trigger):-
Kya karta hai: Yeh tag SailPoint engine ko order deta hai ki, 
"Jaise hi ye Work Item generate ho (yaani form user ki screen/dashboard par aaye), 
to turant us owner ko ek Notification Email bhejo."
Yeh batata hai ki is work item ke aate hi background me email trigger ho jaana chahiye.

3. <Reference class="sailpoint.object.EmailTemplate" name="Work Item Assignment"/>:-
Yeh tag batata hai ki email ke andar kya likha hoga aur wo kaise dikhega. Iske andar do bade attributes hain:-
class="sailpoint.object.EmailTemplate": Yeh SailPoint ko batata hai ki jis cheez ko hum dhoodh rahe hain, 
wo database me ek Email Template object ke roop me save hai.
name="Work Item Assignment": Yeh sabse important hai.Yeh us email template ka asli naam (Unique ID) hai jise SailPoint ke database se uthana hai.
Work Item Assignment SailPoint ka ek default (out-of-the-box) template hota hai. 
Iske andar pehle se likha hota hai: "Dear User, a new work item has been assigned to you.Please log in to complete it."
-------------------------------------------------------
()<entry key="errors" value="ref:validationErrors"/>:-
Is XML line ka kaam hai Form ke upar errors (galtiyo) ko dikhane wala ek panel/box taiyar karna.
Agar user form bharte waqt koi galti karta hai (jaise galat email domain dalna ya galat mobile number format),
to jo bhi error message generate hoga, wo isi line ki wajah se screen par top par dikhai dega.

()<Arg name="response" value="ref:response"/> value kisko bhej raha hai step me?
-->yeh line <Arg name="response" value="ref:response"/> is Confirmation Step (Step 4) ke andar maujood Java/BeanShell Script को
value bhej raha hai, taaki us script ke andar likha if (response != null) waala logic chal sake.
----------------------------------------------------------
()FacesMessage.SEVERITY_INFO (Alert Ka Rang): Yeh SailPoint UI ko batata hai ki message ka nature kya hai. 
SEVERITY_INFO ka matlab hai Information/Success. Iski wajah se SailPoint screen par Hare Rang (Green) ka sunder sa alert box 
banata hai. (Agar yahan SEVERITY_ERROR hota to Lal/Red rang ka box banta).

"Account Invite sent successfully." (Summary): Yeh email ke Subject line ki tarah hai. 
Kuch UI components me yeh message Bold me sabse pehle dikhta hai.

"Account Invite sent successfully." (Detail Text): Yeh message ki main body hai jo user ko popup ke andar poori tarah se padhne
ko milti hai.
--------------------------------
()httpSession.setAttribute("sailpoint.web.PageCodeBase.sessionMessages", myMessages);??
Lekin SailPoint ke Workflow me ek dikqat hoti hai—jab aap form submit karte ho, 
to workflow parde ke peeche background me chala jata hai aur browser ka page poori tarah Redirect/Refresh ho jata hai. 
Us refresh ke chakkar me normal tareeqe se banaye gye messages hawa me ud jaate hain (destroy ho jaate hain) 
aur user ko screen par kuch dikhta hi nahi.
Is dikkat ko khatam karne ke liye aapne yeh masterstroke lagaya:-
-->httpSession: Yeh user ka wo live connection hai jo browser aur Tomcat server ke beech chal raha hai. 
Yeh tab tak zinda rehta hai jab tak user Logout nahi kar deta.
-->"sailpoint.web.PageCodeBase.sessionMessages": Yeh SailPoint ke core UI product ki ek In-built Standard Secret Key hai. 
SailPoint ka UI engine har page load hone par is specific memory pocket ko zaroor check karta hai.
setAttribute(..., myMessages): Aapne apni messages ki list uthai aur seedhe is secret key ke andar browser ki permanent memory me patak (save kar) di.

()Dono Milkar UI Par Kya Kamaal Karte Hain?
Jaise hi aapka ye step complete hoga aur workflow user ko wapas SailPoint ke main dashboard par patke (redirect karega), 
to parde ke peeche ye hota hai:-
--SailPoint ka naya page load hote hi sabse pehle user ke session me is key (sailpoint.web.PageCodeBase.sessionMessages) ko dhoodhta hai.
--Use aapki bheji hui list (myMessages) mil jaati hai.
--UI engine dekhta hai ki andar jo message hai uska type SEVERITY_INFO (Green) hai.
--SailPoint screen par top par ekdum se flash notification popup dikha deta hai: "Account Invite sent successfully."
Aur haan, message dikhane ke theek baad SailPoint khud se is session key ko clear (khali) bhi kar deta hai, 
taaki page dobara refresh karne par wahi message baar-baar na dikhe.
*///////////

1. QuickLink Object (Account Invite QuickLink):-
Isko direct End-User (Banda/Admin) trigger karta hai.
Kaun trigger karta hai: Woh user jo dashboard par baitha hai (End-User ya Admin).
Kab trigger karta hai: Jab banda dashboard par dikhne wale "Create Account Invite" wale button/card par manually click karta hai.
Kaise chalta hai: Iska kaam sirf itna hai ki click hote hi yeh parde ke peeche aapke main Workflow (Self Service View Workflow - Public Officer)
ko call karke active kar deta hai aur launch karne wale bande ki ID (launcher) ko workflow ke andar pass kar deta hai.
XML
<?xml version='1.0' encoding='UTF-8'?>
<!DOCTYPE QuickLink PUBLIC "sailpoint.dtd" "sailpoint.dtd">
<QuickLink action="workflow" category="SelfService" name="Account Invite QuickLink" label="Create Account Invite" messageKey="Create Account Invite">
  <Attributes>
    <Map>
      <!-- 1. Kaunsa workflow chalega click par -->
      <entry key="workflowName" value="Self Service View Workflow - Public Officer"/>
      
      <!-- 2. Kaunsa rule filter karega visibility -->
      <entry key="populationRule" value="Account Invite QuickLink Population Rule"/>
      
      <!-- 3. Launcher mapping taaki workflow ko pata chale kaun submit kar raha hai -->
      <entry key="arguments">
        <value>
          <Map>
            <entry key="launcher" value="launcher"/>
          </Map>
        </value>
      </entry>
    </Map>
  </Attributes>
</QuickLink>
///////////////*
()value="launcher" (SailPoint Ka Dynamic Keyword): Yeh SailPoint UI framework ka ek In-built Reserved Keyword hai. 
Iska kaam hota hai live session se us bande ka username pakadna jisne abhi is "Create Account Invite" wale tile/button par click kiya hai.
Bhai, is QuickLink me bhi launcher ki value SailPoint IIQ ka core framework (backend engine) khud b khud deta hai.
Aapko isme alag se koi value manually type nahi karni padti.
*///////////////
2. QuickLink Population Rule (Account Invite QuickLink Population Rule)
Is rule ko SailPoint ka UI Rendering Engine trigger karta hai.
Kaun trigger karta hai: SailPoint IIQ ka core dashboard/desktop framework.
Kab trigger karta hai: Jab bhi koi user (jaise spadmin ya koi employee) 
apna SailPoint dashboard page open karta hai ya use refresh karta hai.
-->Kaise chalta hai: SailPoint sabhi active QuickLink objects ko check karta hai. 
Jaise hi system aapke is "Account Invite QuickLink" par aata hai, 
woh turant iske andar mapped population rule ko execute karta hai. 
Agar rule true return karega, toh UI par "Create Account Invite" ka button employee ko dikhega, 
agar false return karega toh button chhip (hide) jayega.
XML
<?xml version='1.0' encoding='UTF-8'?>
<!DOCTYPE Rule PUBLIC "sailpoint.dtd" "sailpoint.dtd">
<Rule name="Account Invite QuickLink Population Rule" type="QuickLinkPopulation">
  <Description>Yeh rule control karta hai ki kaunsa user is self-service form ko dekh sakta hai.</Description>
  <Source>
    <![CDATA[
    import sailpoint.object.Identity;

    boolean hasAccess = false;
    if (identity != null) {
        // Kisi bhi valid logged-in user ko yeh button dashboard par dikhega
        hasAccess = true; 
    }
    return hasAccess;
    ]]>
  </Source>
</Rule>

3.Account Invite Core Business Rule (Account Invite):-
Isko aapka Workflow Engine (WorkflowEngine) trigger karta hai.
Kaun trigger karta hai: SailPoint ka Workflow Executor (Internal Step Handler).
Kab trigger karta hai: Jab user form par details (Email aur Mobile) bhar kar "Submit" button daba deta hai 
aur workflow apne agle step par badhta hai.
Kaise chalta hai: Workflow ke andar aapne is step par explicit action likha hua hai: action="rule:Account Invite". 
Jaise hi workflow engine is step par pahunchta hai, woh is Rule ko call karta hai aur form ke saare inputs (email, mobile) 
is rule ke andar java variables ke roop mein inject kar deta hai taaki aapka backend business logic chal sake.
XML
<?xml version='1.0' encoding='UTF-8'?>
<!DOCTYPE Rule PUBLIC "sailpoint.dtd" "sailpoint.dtd">
<Rule name="Account Invite" type="Custom">
  <Description>
    REAL LOGIC: Yeh rule workflow se email aur mobile lekar ek naya Identity Cube (User) 
    bana raha hai, aur use successful hone par system me save karke email trigger karta hai.
  </Description>
  <Source>
    <![CDATA[                                      //]]>
    import java.util.HashMap;
    import java.util.Map;
    import org.apache.commons.lang.StringUtils;
    import sailpoint.object.Identity;
    import sailpoint.object.EmailTemplate;
    import sailpoint.object.EmailOptions;
    import sailpoint.api.SailPointContext;
    import org.apache.commons.logging.Log;
    import org.apache.commons.logging.LogFactory;

    // 1. Production Logs Setup
    Log logger = LogFactory.getLog("custom.rule.AccountInvite");
    logger.info("--- [REAL LOGIC] Account Invite Rule Started ---");

    Map responseMap = new HashMap();
    int statusCode = 500; // Default error state

    try {
        // 2. Workflow variables se data khincha
        String inputEmail = (String) context.getArguments().get("email");
        String inputMobile = (String) context.getArguments().get("mobile");

        if (StringUtils.isNotBlank(inputEmail) && StringUtils.isNotBlank(inputMobile)) {
            
            // Unique Username banana (Misaal ke taur par email ka prefix utha liya)
            // Name: amit@gov.sg -> Username: amit_invite
            String username = inputEmail.substring(0, inputEmail.indexOf("@")) + "_invite";
            
            // 3. Duplicate Check: Kya is username ka banda pehle se SailPoint me hai?
            Identity existingIdentity = context.getObjectByName(Identity.class, username);
            
            if (existingIdentity != null) {
                statusCode = 400; // Bad Request
                responseMap.put("status", "Duplicate");
                responseMap.put("message", "A user with username '" + username + "' or email already exists in SailPoint.");
                logger.warn("Identity already exists for username: " + username);
            } else {
                
                // 4. REAL ACTION: Create New Identity Cube
                Identity newIdentity = new Identity();
                newIdentity.setName(username);
                newIdentity.setFirstname("Invited");
                newIdentity.setLastname("Officer");
                newIdentity.setEmail(inputEmail);
                
                // Custom attribute me mobile number save karna (Maan lijiye aapke system me custom attribute 'mobile' hai)
                newIdentity.setAttribute("mobile", inputMobile);
                
                // User ko system me live (Active) karna
                newIdentity.setInactive(false);
                
                // 5. Save the Identity Object in SailPoint DB
                context.saveObject(newIdentity);
                context.commitTransaction(); // Database me entry locked ho gayi
                logger.info("Successfully created Identity Cube for: " + username);

                // 6. Dhasu Trigger: Use automatic welcome email bhejna
                EmailTemplate template = context.getObjectByName(EmailTemplate.class, "Work Item Assignment"); // Ya aapka koi custom welcome template
                if (template != null) {
                    EmailOptions options = new EmailOptions();
                    options.setTo(inputEmail);
                    
                    // Email ke andar variables pass karne ke liye args map
                    Map emailArgs = new HashMap();
                    emailArgs.put("identityName", username);
                    options.setVariables(emailArgs);
                    
                    // Core SailPoint Email API ko call kiya
                    context.sendEmailNotification(template, options);
                    logger.info("Notification Email sent to: " + inputEmail);
                }

                // Everything is green!
                statusCode = 200;
                responseMap.put("status", "Success");
                responseMap.put("message", "Identity created and invite notification sent successfully.");
            }

        } else {
            statusCode = 400;
            responseMap.put("status", "Error");
            responseMap.put("message", "Required input fields are missing.");
        }

    } catch (Exception e) {
        statusCode = 500;
        responseMap.put("status", "Exception");
        responseMap.put("message", "Backend Exception: " + e.getMessage());
        logger.error("Exception in Account Invite Real Logic: " + e.getMessage(), e);
    }

    // 7. Workflow ko response return kiya
    responseMap.put("statusCode", statusCode);
    logger.info("--- [REAL LOGIC] Account Invite Rule Ended with Status: " + statusCode + " ---");
    return responseMap;
    ]]>
  </Source>
</Rule>
/////////////*
()1. inputEmail.indexOf("@") ── Position Pata Karna:-
Kaam: Yeh string me dhoodhta hai ki @ (at the rate) ka symbol kis number (index) par betha hai. 
Java me counting hamesha 0 se shuru hoti hai.
Misaal: Agar email hai amit@gov.sg:-
a -> 0, m -> 1, i -> 2, t -> 3
@ -> 4 (To indexOf("@") hamein 4 return karega).

2. inputEmail.substring(0, ...) ── Tukda Kaatna:-
Syntax Rule: substring(start_index, end_index) text ko shuru se lekar end waale number ke theek ek akshar pehle tak kaat leta 
hai. (End index waale character ko include nahi karta).
Aapka Case: substring(0, 4) ── Yeh 0 se shuru karega aur 4 (jo ki @ hai) se theek pehle tak ka text kaat lega.
Result: Hamein mil gaya @ ke pehle ka poora naam: "amit".

3. + "_invite" ── Suffix Kyun Joda?
Agar hum sirf email ka pehle ka hissa uthate (amit), to SailPoint me duplicate usernames ka bohot bada khatra ho jata.
Maan lijiye system me pehle se ek permanent employee maujood hai jiska username amit hai. 
Ab aap jab naye user ko invitation bhejenge, to system use duplicate bolkar reject kar deta.
Isliye aapne smart logic lagaya: Uske peeche _invite jod diya.
Ab naya username ban gaya: "amit_invite".
*////////////
-----------------------------------
pehle xml file import kare:-
No. 1: Account Invite QuickLink Population Rule (Pehle population rule)
No. 2: Account Invite Core Business Rule (Phir workflow wala business rule)
No. 3: Mian Workflow XML (Phir apna fixed workflow file)
No. 4: Account Invite QuickLink Object XML (Sabse aakhir mein button config)
Toh Import ke baad chalane ke liye kya karna padega?
Aapko bas Logout karke Dubara Login karna padega

()SailPoint IIQ mein do tarah ke workflows hote hain:-
-->Event-Driven Workflows (Auto-Pilot): Jaise Joiner, Mover, Leaver. Inme jab user ka data badalta hai, tab unhe chalane ke liye Lifecycle Event aur Trigger Rule lagta hai (jaise humne pichle cellphone wale example mein kiya tha).
-->Manual/Self-Service Workflows (QuickLink Tools): Yeh jo aapka "Account Invite" wala workflow hai, yeh tab chalta hai jab koi user khud dashboard par jaakar button par click karta hai.
Chunki yeh button click par chalta hai, isiliye isko chalane ka kaam direct QuickLink XML karta hai, na ki koi Lifecycle Event.
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
/////////////*
Quick Comparison Table:-
Feature                         return Attribute                                    resultVariable Attribute
Kahan use hota hai?---------<Approval> aur <SubWorkflow> tags ke andar.------------<Step> aur <Script> tags ke andar.
Kaam kya hai?----Kisi doosre object (jaise WorkItem ya SubWorkflow) se data ko Parent Workflow mein map karna.---Kisi step ke Script/Rule ka output ek workflow variable mein store karna.
*///////////
////////*
()String Comparison (==): Java/Beanshell mein strings compare karne ke liye == nahi, balki .equals() use hota hai.

()1. Risk kya hai? (status.equals("InActive"))
Agar status ki value null hai, aur aap likhte hain status.equals(...),toh aap aakhirkar null.equals(...) call karne ki koshish kar rahe hain.
Java mein kisi bhi null object par koi method call karne se turant NullPointerException (NPE) aata hai aur aapka rule/workflow wahin crash ho jata hai.

2. Safe tareeka kyun hai? ("InActive".equals(status))
Yahan par "InActive" ek String Literal hai (yaani ek pakka object jo kabhi null nahi ho sakta).
Jab aap "InActive".equals(status) likhte hain, toh .equals() method check karta hai ki andar bheja gaya variable (status) null hai ya nahi.
Agar status null hota hai, toh ye bina crash kiye chupchaap false return kar deta hai.


*/////////
